# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Streams Topology Build to Processor Node Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a Kafka Streams topology is built and compiled to a task graph in apache/kafka. Find Java source files implementing: StreamsBuilder.build(), the InternalTopologyBuilder, the ProcessorTopology, the StoreBuilder registration, and the StreamTask processor node initialization.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Kafka Streams topology build chain. The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` documents:

## Summary

I've traced the complete flow of how a Kafka Streams topology is built and compiled to a task graph:

1. **StreamsBuilder.build()** - The public API entry point that calls `InternalStreamsBuilder.buildAndOptimizeTopology()`

2. **InternalStreamsBuilder.buildAndOptimizeTopology()** - Traverses the logical topology graph and calls `writeToTopology()` on each GraphNode (including StateStoreNode, ProcessorGraphNode, StreamSourceNode, etc.)

3. **InternalTopologyBuilder.addStateStore()** - Registers state stores via StoreFactory instances in the stateFactories map (lines 602-627)

4. **InternalTopologyBuilder.buildTopology()** - Initiates the physical topology construction (lines 963-973)

5. **InternalTopologyBuilder.build()** - Core method that:
   - Builds ProcessorNodes from NodeFactory.build()
   - **Builds StateStores** via `storeFactory.builder().build()` (line 1146)
   - Builds SourceNodes and SinkNodes
   - Constructs ProcessorTopology with all components (lines 1052-1059)

6. **StreamTask.initializeTopology()** - Initializes each ProcessorNode by calling `node.init(processorContext, processingExceptionHandler)` (lines 1080-1091)

The answer includes detailed file paths, symbol locations, and a narrative explaining the store builder registration pipeline and how the topology flows from high-level DSL to initialized processor nodes ready for execution.

This also means that the work\\n188:      * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\\n189:      * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\\n190:      * <p>\\n191:      * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\\n192:      * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\\n193:      * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\\n194:      *\\n195:      * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\\n196:      * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\\n197:      */\\n198:     public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\\n199:         return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\\n200:     }\\n201: \\n202:     /**\\n203:      * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\\n204:      * The {@code \\\"auto.offset.reset\\\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\\n205:      * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\\n206:      * <p>\\n207:      * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\\n208:      * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics. \\n516: \\n517:     /**\\n518:      * Adds a state store to the underlying {@link Topology}.\\n519:      * <p>\\n520:      * It is required to connect state stores to {@link import java.util.regex.Pattern;\n48: \n49: /**\n50:  * {@code StreamsBuilder} provides the high-level Kafka Streams DSL to specify a Kafka Streams topology.\n51:  *\n52:  * <p>\n53:  * It is a This also means that the work\n188:      * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n189:      * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\n190:      * <p>\n191:      * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n192:      * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n193:      * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n194:      *\n195:      * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\n196:      * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n197:      */\n198:     public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\n199:         return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\n200:     }\n201: \n202:     /**\n203:      * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\n204:      * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n205:      * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n206:      * <p>\n207:      * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\n208:      * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics. // key must be local (application state is shared over all running Kafka Streams instances)\n256:      * }</pre>\n257:      * For non-local keys, a custom RPC mechanism must be implemented using {@link KafkaStreams#metadataForAllStreamsClients()} to\n258:      * query the value of the key on a parallel running instance of your Kafka Streams application.\n259:      *\n260:      * @param topic              the topic name; Constructs new ProcessorTopology with:\\n     - List of built ProcessorNodes\\n     - Map of source nodes by topic\\n     - Map of sink nodes by topic\\n     - List of built StateStores\\n     - List of global state stores\\n     - User calls `StreamsBuilder.addStateStore(StoreBuilder)` or uses materialized operators\\n2. `StreamsBuilder.addStateStore()` calls `internalStreamsBuilder.addStateStore(StoreBuilderWrapper.wrapStoreBuilder(builder))` (line 530)\\n3. `InternalStreamsBuilder.addStateStore()` creates `StateStoreNode(builder)` and adds it to the graph (line 220)\\n4. During buildAndOptimizeTopology, `StateStoreNode.writeToTopology(internalTopologyBuilder)` is called\\n5. This calls `internalTopologyBuilder.addStateStore(storeBuilder)` (StateStoreNode line 35)\\n6. `InternalTopologyBuilder.addStateStore()` stores the StoreFactory in the `stateFactories` map (line 617)\\n7. During `build()`, when processing processor nodes that reference the store:\\n   - The StoreFactory is retrieved from `stateFactories` (line 1131)\\n   - `storeFactory.builder().build()` is called to create the actual StateStore instance (line 1146)\\n   - The store is added to `stateStoreMap` (line 1147)\\n   - The store is passed to ProcessorTopology constructor\\n\\n## Summary\\nThe topology compilation follows a clear separation of concerns: The DSL layer (StreamsBuilder, InternalStreamsBuilder) manages the logical topology graph, the InternalTopologyBuilder layer constructs physical node factories and builds the actual ProcessorTopology with initialized stores, and finally the StreamTask layer initializes processor nodes for runtime execution. Store builders are registered early and built just-in-time when the ProcessorTopology is constructed, allowing for proper configuration and integration with changelog topics.\"\n}\n",
